< text>
A good place to take your pet to have them checked up on, but know more fees will apply than the visit fee so make sure you ask up front.  I took my pet in to get some more pain pills for her arthritis in her hips.  Her pills had ran out and I called in to get the prescription refilled.  They said I would only have to pay the visit fee.  Once I got in and seen the vet, they tell me they have to take blood work, etc. to refill her pain meds.  This is when I find out it will cost me over $200 for the blood work and they cant refill her meds without it.  Suffice to say I just paid the visit fee for absolutely nothing.  Left with no pain meds for my dog and upset I was not told up front what would be necessary to have her prescription refilled.  I would have came when I had $200+ to get more pain meds.  No transparency!< /text>

< Review>
I was looking for a Subaru mechanic for my 2006 Outback, which after 130,000 miles had an engine that was leaking oil, stinking up the inside with a bad smell, and developing other mechanical problems.  I had it checked out with a different repair shop I've used for my other cars, but this time it seemed like they didn't quite know what they were doing.  I was finally informed that I needed a new head gasket, which is a big expensive ($2500) job.  After making some phone calls,  I was pleased to discover that Sacramento Specialty Automotive could offer me a higher quality gasket and do the work I needed to have done for $500 less than either my regular repair shop or the Subaru dealer.  To boot, they did my timing belt and water pump, cleaned up some corrosion, changed other minor gaskets, and replaced my air filter and spark plugs for no added labor cost.  While the major work was underway, I was able to add a brake job and have some needed front suspension work done (bushings and ball joints) with the money I saved by choosing this repair facility.   Now my car no longer leaks, no longer stinks, and drives like when I bought it.  No one, including me, likes to spend $3,000 on auto repairs.  However, since a Subaru can last for 250,000 miles, I believe in the long run, it's more economical to fix it than to replace it.  The guys at Sacramento Specialty Automotive communicated well with me at every step of the process, and are super-efficient in what they do.  They inspected my vehicle, sent me a detailed report with photos, got the engine out of the car and disassembled, had critical parts machined, reassembled the engine, put it back in the car and road tested it in under four days.  Who can do that anymore?  These guys are professionals who know the Subaru and understand what they are doing.  If I ever need serious work done on my Outback again, this is where I'm taking it.<//Review>

<Text>Casual, local family-run, simple, Americana burger joint with formal, 'please-wait-to-be-seated' restaurant prices...
Pros: Burger was cooked just right and tasted spectacular! The fries are fresh and you get a lot of 'em! The outdoor seating in the garden is really a nice place to eat on a nice day, with lots of tables and plenty of room. The staff is friendly and the food was ready in not much time at all.
Cons: They do not offer, make or sell milkshakes. All in all, the main aspect of my visit that caught me off guard the most was, my bill. The food is rather expensive. A burger with fries, ordered together as a "meal" is just that, a burger and fries, nothing else. So, a meal, plus a regular soft drink (self serve, so refills are included) rounded out to just about 15 dollars, add the tip because the service was good and my regular sized 'order-for-one' ran me close to 20 bucks! IMHO, If I was able to order a regular milkshake (or better yet, a malt) with my burger and fries, then I would have expected a decent sized check. But hey, prices are only gonna keep getting higher, and you really can't get any more Americana than that... Maybe this is a sign that I'm officially 'getting old'.... üôÅ ...
